  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_af16060a-8bf9-4031-877d-e2296fbe3c0d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1223923802199209630">As a Red, Darrow grew up working the mines deep beneath the surface of Mars, enduring backbreaking labor while dreaming of the better future he was building for his descendants. But the Society he faithfully served was built on lies. Darrow’s kind have been betrayed and denied by their elitist masters, the Golds—and their only path to liberation is revolution.   <span id="freeText1223923802199209630" style="display:none">As a Red, Darrow grew up working the mines deep beneath the surface of Mars, enduring backbreaking labor while dreaming of the better future he was building for his descendants. But the Society he faithfully served was built on lies. Darrow’s kind have been betrayed and denied by their elitist masters, the Golds—and their only path to liberation is revolution. And so Darrow sacrifices himself in the name of the greater good for which Eo, his true love and inspiration, laid down her own life. He becomes a Gold, infiltrating their privileged realm so that he can destroy it from within. <br /><br />A lamb among wolves in a cruel world, Darrow finds friendship, respect, and even love—but also the wrath of powerful rivals. To wage and win the war that will change humankind’s destiny, Darrow must confront the treachery arrayed against him, overcome his all-too-human desire for retribution—and strive not for violent revolt but a hopeful rebirth. Though the road ahead is fraught with danger and deceit, Darrow must choose to follow Eo’s principles of love and justice to free his people. <br /><br />He must live for more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1223923802199209630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/36300889-johnny-wenzel"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_100x100-c7bfe730633c9983e27caaa66a8e244a.png" /></a>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/36300889-johnny-wenzel">Johnny Wenzel</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Pierce Brown mentioned that he pictured Fitchner to be Paul Bettany (Knight's Tale, Beautiful Mind), but I don't really see it. <br/><br/>I could go with Rhys W<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Pierce Brown mentioned that he pictured Fitchner to be Paul Bettany (Knight's Tale, Beautiful Mind), but I don't really see it. <br /><br />I could go with Rhys Wakefield. Handsome enough to be a gold but villainy enough to be Sevro.<br /><br />I would love to see Emma Watson play Mustang. She usually takes the smart girl role, but I think she could pull off Mustang's edge very well.<br /><br />Alex Pettyfur for Cassius<br /><br />Marie Avgeropoulos for Antonia<br /><br />Darrow....is impossible. I picture someone like Robbie Amell but I think they should take someone unknown for him. I wouldn't want a celebrity to detract from who Darrow is. For example, initially, I saw Katniss as Katniss but now I just see Jennifer Lawrence. I couldn't buy into Dan Brown's Robert Langdon because all I could see was Tom Hanks (don't get me wrong; I love both movie series, but I'd like to experience Darrow with a new face). <br /><br />I clearly liked this question. More people should pitch in thoughts.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<a href="/questions/363666-anyone-else-not-convinced-by-roque-s"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Anyone else not convinced by Roque's betrayal? I know it was set up, and it was to be expected. However it just doesn't quite make sense with the character. Roque is a poet, if anyone would stand with Darrow in his mission to blend the colors it would be him. I just don't see him reacting the way that he did and it smells like he is part of this to actually help Darrow. What do you guys think? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1553302362" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1553302362" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1553302362?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1553302362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3951394707146572679"><blockquote>
  <i>“I will die. You will die. We will all die and the universe will carry on without care. All that we have is that shout into the wind - how we live. How we go. And how we stand before we fall.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>I *almost* didn't write a review for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18966819.Golden_Son__Red_Rising___2_' title='Golden Son (Red Rising, #2) by Pierce Brown' rel='nofollow noopener'>Golden Son</a>. It doesn't matter how many reviews I write or how snarky I've been in the past, there is something extremely intimidating about writing a negative review for a book that all my friends loved, that critics praised, and that has an average Goodreads rating </span>
  <span id="freeText3951394707146572679" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“I will die. You will die. We will all die and the universe will carry on without care. All that we have is that shout into the wind - how we live. How we go. And how we stand before we fall.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I *almost* didn't write a review for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18966819.Golden_Son__Red_Rising___2_" title="Golden Son (Red Rising, #2) by Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Golden Son</a>. It doesn't matter how many reviews I write or how snarky I've been in the past, there is something extremely intimidating about writing a negative review for a book that all my friends loved, that critics praised, and that has an average Goodreads rating of 4.49. I spent some time actually trying to come up with what was wrong with me as a way of explanation.<br /><br />It must be me, right? I must not have appreciated it right. It must be the wrong time. I must be hormonal. Because I just <b>DO NOT GET IT</b>. In the last week alone, I've had multiple requests from people telling me to continue with this series, calling it "one of the best series ever", and saying <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18966819.Golden_Son__Red_Rising___2_" title="Golden Son (Red Rising, #2) by Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Golden Son</a> is so much better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839976.Red_Rising__Red_Rising___1_" title="Red Rising (Red Rising, #1) by Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Rising</a>.<br /><br />Is it? <br /><br />Because I struggle to see the leap between the two. So many reviewers have acknowledged that Darrow was the very definition of a Gary Stu in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839976.Red_Rising__Red_Rising___1_" title="Red Rising (Red Rising, #1) by Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Rising</a>, and yet many are now citing his epic failure at the start of this book as evidence of him shedding the Gary Stu-ness. But I just don't buy it. Even when he fails, he fails like a damn hero with fireworks going off behind his head, rushing back to rescue a damsel in distress in true, self-sacrificing perfection.<br /><br />Even when he fails, he doesn't fail.<br />Even when things are awful, he has to deliver a melodramatic, rousing speech.<br /><br /><b>Darrow is possibly the most self-obsessed <s>character</s> caricature I have ever come across</b>. He loves to hear himself speak - or think, as it may be.<br /><br />There's a word - <i>arch</i> - that's used in various contexts, but is often used in theatre and acting as an example of how not to act. It refers to delivering lines while mentally side-eying the audience with a visible self-awareness of the part you are playing and what comes next. For example, playing out a dramatic scene with visible knowledge of your next line. Darrow feels like that. I feel like he is reading off a script. Every dramatic speech and inner monologue does not feel like someone making a realistically important speech in the face of death, it feels like a bad actor dramatically wiping his brow, doing a Sally Field lip bite, and launching into his lines.<br /><br />He's not really scared because duh, he's playing Darrow, he knows he can't fail in the end.<br /><br />Not only is he an epic drama llama, but he is still the voice of insufferably good and just morality. On one side, he has the Sons of Ares willing to go to extreme terrorist lengths for their cause, and on the other side he has many cold, callous Golds who DNGAF about the lower classes. Many times it feels like Darrow is the only one allowed to care about anything and allowed to be upset about the deaths of innocents.<br /><br />Even the most interesting character (by far) feels so unnatural and out of place in the story. Everyone is saluting Mustang as this amazing, strong female who completely overwrites the issues the last book introduced (i.e. all female characters are useless and need saving) and yet she does indeed feel like a direct response to readers' concerns. Her most memorable scene is a feminist speech she makes about being super smart and unapologetic and I can't help thinking... Brown is going for the female vote. <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B55DR7Zgn_A" rel="nofollow noopener">Because we all know how much he loves to milk that</a>.<br /><br />And, in a sea of books about civil unrest and divides between ruling/slave classes, I think the only way the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839976.Red_Rising__Red_Rising___1_" title="Red Rising (Red Rising, #1) by Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Rising</a> trilogy stands out is by its heavier use of scientific language and technical descriptions. I don't feel like it does anything different in terms of plot or characters.<br /><br />I lack the ability to care what will happen going forward. I feel like there is literally nothing I’m reading for… I don’t care how the war ends, I don’t care if Darrow lives or dies, I don’t care about any relationships. There are just no answers I’m seeking from this series. Which is why I won't be reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18966806.Morning_Star__Red_Rising___3_" title="Morning Star (Red Rising, #3) by Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Morning Star</a>, no matter how many people tell me I should.<br /><br />Seriously, though, who talks like this (note: this isn't Darrow):<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“… I was in a dark woods, blind and lost as Dante before Virgil. But Quinn helped me. Her voice calling me out of misery. She became my home. As she puts it, “Home isn’t where you’re from, it’s where you find light when all grows dark.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3951394707146572679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4514434660043416969">Did I mention that I listened to these almost exclusively as audiobooks?<br/><br/>I did. And the narration was, to put it plainly, purely brilliant. Dude knocked it out of the park.<br/><br/>In fact, the narrative voice was so strong that when I picked up a paper copy of the book so I could read it faster. (I read about 5 or 6 times faster off the page.) The narrator's voice stuck with me in my head, like when you read some text next to a picture of Morgan Freeman.<br/><br/>So yeah. Not just some excellent books. But excelle</span>
  <span id="freeText4514434660043416969" style="display:none">Did I mention that I listened to these almost exclusively as audiobooks?<br /><br />I did. And the narration was, to put it plainly, purely brilliant. (I read about 5 or 6 times faster off the page.) The narrator's voice stuck with me in my head, like when you read some text next to a picture of Morgan Freeman.<br /><br />So yeah. Not just some excellent books. But excellent audio production as well. </span>

This book is all over the place with everything! <br><br>Blowing people up in space, bloody battles, stupidity, more people being blown up here and there and everywhere! People you like getting killed. People you don't like that you want to beat into the ground! <br><br>Oh and the part with Darrow and his mom made me cry! <br><br>Let me just add some random excerpts that have to do with Darrow and Sevro and stuff! <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I explode through the bridge like a ball of lead shot into a store of china and glass. I crash into displays and strategy desks before blasting through the reinforced metal of the bridge walls, through the steel of the hallways till at last I slam bodily into a bulkhead a hundred meters through and past the bridge. Dazed. Can't find Sevro. I call him over the com. He groans something about his ass. Maybe he did shit himself.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Okay, so here is a moment that Darrow and Sevro had together after finding out a revelation. It brought a tear to my eye for reasons, there's always reasons people. Well, the tear to my eye came after the first part and some stuff and then the other stuff =D<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Sevro spits in my face, right under the eye. "Guess wrong again and I leave you like this." He snaps his fingers. "I will not come back. I will not help you. I will not bleed for you. I will not sacrifice my friends for a man who doesn't give enough of a shit about me to put his neck out just once. Trust goes both ways, Darrow. This time you have to take a leap."</blockquote>
</b><br><br>shfosehgsoihgsiodhfsidfhsifh some stuff and. . . <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>He can't say any more because I'm hugging him and crying. I sob and hold on to him, shaking, scaring him. He doesn't move except to pat me on the head. All the weight falls from my shoulders. Someone knows. He knows and he's here. He knows and he came to help me. To help me. I can't stop shaking and saying thank you. Eo was right. I was right. "You are my friend," I tremble out like a child. It almost makes him cry seeing me this way.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Once again, that ending! I can't even! It was messed right up and sad but good. We can't have it all! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1557852788i/27506971._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Happy Reading! <br><br>Mel 🖤🐶🐺🐾<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2018/01/golden-son-by-pierce-brown.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16342773510300520951">ready for a little biology lesson? goosebumps are a fight or flight response. usually (weather excluded), they occur when experiencing intense emotions towards something and adrenaline is released throughout the body.<br/><br/>so what does it say about this book that i had goosebumps pretty much throughout the entire thing?? it means this book is straight up chilling and, good gosh, i am in utter disbelief right now. i honestly dont know if i finished this book or if it finished me. thats how im feeling r</span>
  <span id="freeText16342773510300520951" style="display:none">ready for a little biology lesson? goosebumps are a fight or flight response. usually (weather excluded), they occur when experiencing intense emotions towards something and adrenaline is released throughout the body.<br /><br />so what does it say about this book that i had goosebumps pretty much throughout the entire thing?? it means this book is straight up chilling and, good gosh, i am in utter disbelief right now. i honestly dont know if i finished this book or if it finished me. thats how im feeling right now.<br /><br />the range of emotions i felt whilst reading this is exhausting. i feel like a wet towel that has been wrung out for every last drop of water. i never knew i could feel so much. i am R E E L I N G.<br /><br />ps. i still think pierce brown is a total hottie and, after reading this, im pretty sure im in love. &lt;3<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>5 stars</i></b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1777899610" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1777899610" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1777899610?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444759037" href="/book/show/25372230-golden-son">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Sci-Fi &amp; Space Opera fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59458347-petrik?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1777899610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8599748835333780535">Buddy reading this book with my favorite Howlers: <br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/La_Luna_Moonchild' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sarah</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/celeste57' rel='nofollow noopener'>Celeste</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/ravageroftomes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mary</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/35431290-tweebs' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tweebie</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/35147071-jenn-the-dark-lord-scribe-house-of-slytheread' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jennymort</a><br/><br/><b>Take all these 5 stars from me, Pierce Brown, take it, you completely deserve it. </b><br/><br/>Unbelievable… It wasn’t an exaggeration when literally everyone told me the sequels to Red Rising are much better, Golden Son is truly an incredible installment in the trilogy. I praised Red Rising, I enjoyed reading it so much and yet it pales in comparison to its sequel. I started reading Golden Son on 8th January, the day I</span>
  <span id="freeText8599748835333780535" style="display:none">Buddy reading this book with my favorite Howlers: <br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/La_Luna_Moonchild" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/celeste57" rel="nofollow noopener">Celeste</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/ravageroftomes" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/35431290-tweebs" rel="nofollow noopener">Tweebie</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/35147071-jenn-the-dark-lord-scribe-house-of-slytheread" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennymort</a><br><br><b>Take all these 5 stars from me, Pierce Brown, take it, you completely deserve it. </b><br><br>Unbelievable… It wasn’t an exaggeration when literally everyone told me the sequels to Red Rising are much better, Golden Son is truly an incredible installment in the trilogy. I praised Red Rising, I enjoyed reading it so much and yet it pales in comparison to its sequel. I started reading Golden Son on 8th January, the day I turned 28, finished it in 3 days and <b>I’m so lucky to have chosen this book to be my first read in my new age.</b><br><br>There’s a new contender for the biggest lie I ever heard and that’s seeing this book shelved under <i>“YA”</i>. I was reluctant to start this series because of it (yes, I'm not a fan of YA) but I'm really glad that didn't stop me. Forget all the similarity with other YA books you think you’ve seen or heard in Red Rising, you won’t find any of them here at all. It completely goes into <b>adult military sci-fi territory</b> and written like one. No sugar coating, there’s a lot of harsh words, bloodbaths, brutality and some gore here. Unless your 13 old kids have their balls or tits tempered with Thor’s hammer, I recommend you to make them stay away from this book. It’s up to you in the end though, who knows? Maybe your kids will learn how to defy their bullies with Lego after reading this book since there are a lot of strategy and badasses involved here.<br><br>Whether you’re one of those who loved (like me) or hated the previous book because of the plot, I’ll assure you that this time the plot took off in a completely different direction than before and it’s so much better. <b>It relies on the foundation laid by the first book to hurl the plot itself to become a massive sci-fi and space opera (literally from page 1). Packed with non-stop actions, politics, bloody space or ground warfare and twists and turns, it will truly grip you right from the beginning until the end.</b> Seriously, there are only a few chapters where you’re allowed to take a break before the story pulls you into all the madness and blood feud again.<br><br>Have I mentioned the ending is so mind-blowing it's designed to give you an anxiety attack? <b>I strongly recommend you to have MORNING STAR <i>(Last book of the trilogy)</i> beside you before you finished the book.</b> It’s probably one of the most fucked up cliffhangers I ever experienced in my whole life. <i>(I’m actually typing this review after I read the first 2 chapter of Morning Star straight after finishing Golden Son, otherwise this review will consist only of me typing my foamy mouth into words “argh urgh fruha euehoqo dsuhckijk quhaorj uhjqpkco”.)</i><br><br>Frankly, I didn’t expect myself to get attached to the characters in this book so much when I started the series but I do, I really do. I’m a huge sucker for great character developments. I love when there is an improvement in the characters personality, strength and weaknesses and changes in all their relationships. Whether it’s in the form of love blossomed or betrayal casted, as long as they’re executed perfectly and make sense, I’ll never get tired of them and this book has them all. <br><br>There are some new great characters here, Ragnar <i>(not Lothbrok)</i>, Victra and Lorn specifically but my favorite part will have to be seeing the relationship development between Darrow and his best friends, old and new, especially Sevro. These two friendships are what I’d definitely called #friendshipgoals, they understand each other, bantered carelessly and most of all loyal to each other. Sadly I can’t tell you much more on this part this time as there are a lot of factors that I think would be much better for you to experience it yourself rather than hearing it from me but I’ll let you know that Darrow and Sevro are definitely my favorite and the best characters in the book for me.<br><br><b>Darrow</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484246017i/21699515._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Sevro’s re-introduction</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484045422i/21676027._SY540_.jpg" width='400"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The world-building scale is bigger than before as this time we deal with space travel and worlds hopping. It’s much easier to read and imagine compare to before as almost all the info dump was established already in the first book. This time, none of the world-building felt like Earth anymore and that’s a huge plus for me, I don’t want my head to imagine Earth when the settings are clearly not.<br><br>I mentioned before in my Red Rising review that I absolutely loved Pierce Brown’s writing, it still holds true here, in fact, I love it even more now as I really think he really improved his writing style. It’s much more engrossing, immersive, poetic and yet still retained all the previous elements that captivated me.<br><br> There are also a lot of great one-liners and fantastic quotes which will give you hope, laughter or something to think upon when you go through the book, here are some of my favorites:<br><br><b>
  <i>“I will die. You will die. We will all die and the universe will carry on without care. All that we have is that shout into the wind - how we live. How we go. And how we stand before we fall.”</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>“Home isn't where you're from, it's where you find light when all grows dark.”</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>“Friendships take minutes to make, moments to break, years to repair.”</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>"I'm Gold, bitch. What'd you expect? Warm milk and cookies just because I'm pocket sized?”</i>
</b><br><br>Adrenaline inducement is imminent, words you read will shoot straight to your heart and fill your feelings with love towards the main and side characters, rage and hatred towards the villains. Betrayal, bloodydamn epic action and military warfare <i>(ground and space)</i> sequences are written so vivid it felt like I’m experiencing a much more epic and dark version of Star Wars/Trek <i>(yes I said that, deal with it).</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483848602ra/21655534.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’m putting this entry into my favorite shelves. Golden Son is everything I ever wanted in a Sci-Fi book, Pierce Brown himself said this is his favorite book out of the trilogy and I really don’t think the 3rd book could top this one but it still remains to be seen. I can say with confidence though that if Morning Star didn’t disappoint, this series will definitely become one of my favorite series of all time. <br><br><b>I urge you strongly to start this series if you love any of these: Sci-fi, space opera, great actions, fantastic climax, great characterization with strong plot, perfect pacing or if you’re eager get your adrenaline fix, hey you don’t need to ride an extreme roller coaster, look no further, read this book and you’ll get all these experience for hours.</b> I may sound calm in my review but inside my burning heart I’m typing this review with fingers full of adrenaline rush from the endless <i>“one more chapter”</i> syndrome this book gave me. This book is the kind of drug I need in this world where sometimes, we simply need a portal to escape from our boring reality and I <i>bloodydamn</i> hope you will experience this as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8599748835333780535" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1129489973" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1129489973" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1129489973?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21425079-golden-son">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone and their brother</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=buddy-reads-are-the-best">buddy-reads-are-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=cover-whore">cover-whore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=it-burns-us-precious">it-burns-us-precious</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1129489973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4192989537160342561"><b>Updated Review:</b><br/><br/>I have this quirk . . . I call it my "false sense of urgency." <br/><br/>It sometimes makes me impatient and unforgiving when I'm reading a book for the first time, and if the new book happens to be the latest installment of one of my favorite series, the possibility of that first read suffering the effects of my FSoU goes up exponentially.<br/><br/>*glances sheepishly at GOLDEN SON* <br/><br/>1. I don't care about the bloody Ash Lord.<br/><br/>2. There was TONS of info about Obsidians and Stained, it just wasn't the in</span>
  <span id="freeText4192989537160342561" style="display:none"><b>Updated Review:</b><br><br>I have this quirk . . . I call it my "false sense of urgency." <br><br>It sometimes makes me impatient and unforgiving when I'm reading a book for the first time, and if the new book happens to be the latest installment of one of my favorite series, the possibility of that first read suffering the effects of my FSoU goes up exponentially.<br><br>*glances sheepishly at GOLDEN SON* <br><br>1. I don't care about the bloody Ash Lord.<br><br>2. There was TONS of info about Obsidians and Stained, it just wasn't the info I wanted, so I threw a temper tantrum.<br><br>3. The sequence that I felt heavily resembled a sequence from STAR TREK INTO DARKNESS . . . I don't know if it was b/c I had watched the movie just prior to reading it, or if it was another byproduct of FSoU, but this time . . . Yeah, it didn't bother me at all. *shrugs awkwardly*<br><br>4. I downplayed it in my original review, but I was also extremely aggravated by Darrow continuing to keep his friends at arms-length, even as he recognized the damage his withholding was causing to those relationships.<br><br>On this second pass, not only did it no longer feel redundant and obstinately foolish, but the friend I most resented being kept at a distance came across as petulant and self-righteous (more about that it the spoiler-tagged section).<br><br>Funnily enough, before my reread, I thought I might have to lower the rating (to 4.0 from 4.5) now that the post-first-read-high had worn off.<br><br>Instead I'm raising it to 5.0. <br><br><b>SPOILERY FINAL THOUGHTS:</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[1. I'm sorry, but Roque is a little bitch. Where the hell does he get off blaming Darrow for their friends' deaths? <br><br>Eff you, dude. Efffff youuuuuu.<br><br>Quinn's a big girl. She--and everyone else who got involved--understood what they were signing up for: CHALLENGING THE SOVEREIGN. No one is responsible for her death except for Aja (also a bitch). <br><br>As for Tactus, he was a turncoat who had to be talked down from murdering Lorn's GRANDCHILDREN. I'm not saying I didn't hurt for him. I did. I hate that he was so screwed up by his upbringing that he couldn't . . . just let himself be. <br><br>But it was no one's fault but his own that he bit it.<br><br>2. Obviously, in light of all that I'm no longer holding out hope that Roque is some kind of double agent . . . <br><br>*grimaces* Sorry, Robin . . . It made sense when we talked about it last year, but not a chance in hell. Hopefully by the time you finish your reread, you'll think he's a prat, too. *crosses fingers*<br><br>3. <blockquote><i>“I found out later, Nero contrived an agreement with the daughter of the sitting Sovereign. You know her as Octavia au Lune. Younger then, she convinced her father to give Nero the throne of Mars and his revenge; in return, she earned Nero’s support when she led the faction that overthrew and killed her father five years later. That is the man you started a war for.”</i></blockquote>
<br>HOLY SHIT.<br><br>4. <blockquote><i>“Narol … is he …?” <br>“Dead? Aye. He’s dead.” <br>The breath goes out of me. “How long?” <br>“Two years ago,” she chuckles. “Fell down a mineshaft with Loran. Never found the bodies.”</i></blockquote>
<br>I'm with Darrow's mamma--I'll believe it when I see their dead bodies.<br><br>5. <blockquote>
<i>“Then farewell hope, and with hope farewell fear. Farewell remorse: all good to me is lost.” </i>He whispers to some distant, fading part of himself as he lazily lifts the scorcher to his father’s forehead. <i>“Evil, be thou my good.” </i><br>“Stop!” Aja steps forward. “Adrius! In the name of the Sovereign …” <br>The Jackal shoots his father in the head.</blockquote>
<br>There is something so <i>sinister</i> about Jackal quoting Lucifer's lines from PARADISE LOST, like he's at <i>that moment</i> becoming a fallen angel. <br><br>Dude, you've been an evil bastard your whole life. Or at least since you were TEN and arranged the death of YOUR BROTHER. <br><br>GTFO.<br><br>PS: I swear to god, if Antonia, Cassius, and Jackal don't die, and by "die" I mean die <i>horribly</i>, there's gonna be 'percussions. Roque, too. Maybe . . . Probably . . . <br><br>DEATH COUNT:<br><br>Quinn<br>Tactus <br>Bellonas, excepting Cassius and his evil mother<br>Pliny <br>Victra <br>Lorn<br>Augustus<br>Fitchner/ARES <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/01/review-golden-son-by-pierce-brown.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>Right. SO . . . after finishing GOLDEN SON did I:<br><br>A. Shriek incomprehensibly. Over and over (and over) again.<br>B. Sit in a semi-comatose state staring at nothing for an indefinite period of time.<br>C. Explain (in detail) to my poor mother (whom I was visiting) EXACTLY what my problem was, despite her having never read either book from this series, and thus being unable to understand what I was ranting about.<br><br>That was a rhetorical question. Obviously, I did them all.<br><br>Pierce Brown, (handsome) devil that he is, lured us into a false sense of security in RED RISING. He taught us that, yes, Bad Things would happen--LOTS of Bad Things--but by the end, we'd have found our footing. We'd know that there was more coming--and HOORAY for that--but the individual installment would be resolved&lt;------LIES.<br><br>But there is far more to GOLDEN SON than it's epic cliffhanger of DOOM.<br><br>In fact, if it weren't for a few minor issues, I'd say it was even better than RED RISING, which tied for first place on my Best Books of 2014 list.<br><br>GOLDEN SON continues to reveal the complexity of Darrow's situation: a Red who is a Gold/a Gold who is a Red. <br><br>What Darrow originally imagined as a simple infiltration and sabotage mission has become infinitely more complicated, and where his hard-learned lessons from RED RISING were painful, his mistakes in this newest installment are downright agonizing. <br><br>He makes those mistakes in both his personal and professional life, while you are forced to watch helplessly. <br><br>You watch helplessly as Darrow enters into an alliance with Jackal, and visions of<br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421086526i/13320213.jpg" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>dance through your head.<br><br>You watch helplessly as Darrow continually keeps his friends at a distance, even as he acknowledges the potentially irreparable damage to the relationships.<br><br>You watch helplessly as the chaos of battle ensues, knowing something . . . something <em>terrible</em> . . . is about to happen.<br><br>And yet, once again, Brown was able to offset the trepidation and dread he made you carry along like travel companions with both well-placed hilarity, like Kavax au Telemanus, who feeds his pet fox jellybeans, and also with fascinating new details about the caste system Darrow is trying to overthrow, like a branch of Obsidians referred to as Stained.<br><br>So it was fantastic. GOLDEN SON will probably be my favorite book in 2015. <br><br>BUT. <br><br>While Brown's ability to paint truly vivid pictures, and to elicit real emotions remains uncompromised, several details were still unclear to me by the end of book.<br><br><b>The Ash Lord</b>. I did a word search in both books and found that, yes, he had been mentioned briefly in RED Rising as having nuked the world of Rhea into oblivion, and as being the minion of Octavia au Lune, the Sovereign Consul. Various mentions are made to his burning and pillaging in GOLDEN SON as well, but always in a seemingly offhand way so that I never really grasped what was supposed to be so terrifying about the man. <br><br>Yes, cerebrally I can comprehend that destroying an entire planet is a terrible thing, but I need meaningful details for something to matter, and in reference to the Ash Lord, there were none. <br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421086526i/13320214.jpg" width="500" height="316" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>Then again, watching Alderaan get blown to bits never made much of dent either, so maybe I'm a sociopath. *shrugs*<br><br>BUT. <br><br>Yes, I was fascinated by them, but I was never satisfied with the introduction of <b>the Stained</b>. <br><br>As far as we've been told, there are two kinds of Reds: underground slaves like Darrow, and those who live above ground and work as menial laborers. The distinction may or may not be arbitray (I have suspicions, but that's for another time). There are also several types of Golds, but the separations are self-imposed and based on achievement, or lack thereof, and are explained as such. If there are deviations within the other colors, we have yet to learn of them.<br><br>And yet, the Stained, a subdivision of Obsidians, are tossed at us as elite bodyguards without explanation. Elite bodyguards, who like the Ash Lord, inspire fear with only the mention of their name. In the first half of the book, they are an almost constant background presence . . . in the retinue of some Gold or another . . . making everyone inexplicably nervous . . . and then we find out why: <br><br>Ragnar Volarus.<br><br>Ragnar Volarus, "<em>a dread creature stitched from shadow and muscle and armor, </em>" and who is, incidentally, one of my new favorite characters. If there are any WHEEL OF TIME fans out there, Ragnar reminded me a lot of that honkin' myrddraal, Shaidar Haran. For the rest of you, that means he's a Stained to make even other Stained quake with fear, who seems capable of intelligent and independent thought, unlike other Obsidians and Stained who simply follow orders. <br><br>But regardless, we never learn the reason for the divide between Obsidian and Stained, and while that may seem a small thing, for an OCD reader (like myself), every, single time I read the word "Stained" on a page, and every, single time Ragnar was present, in the not-so-back of my mind, I was screaming, "Why? Why, why, whyyyyyy?" <br><br>It was a consistent distraction. <br><br>And I'm not going to harp on it, b/c nobody else (that I talked to) even picked up on it, but the scenario where we first met Ragnar . . . It (to me) bore a striking similarity to a certain memorable scene in STAR TREK INTO DARKNESS. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Okay, I'm sorry. I tried really, really hard to let it go, but not only did Darrow and Servo shoot through space in nothing but spacesuits to infiltrate an enemy vessel, but once they got there, Ragnar crushed someone's head with his bare hands. Like a grape. *shudders* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>But all of those are piddly complaints. The only reason they warrant mentioning at all (except the STAR TREK thing, b/c that really bugged me), is b/c they are the reason I'm giving GOLDEN SON 4.5 stars instead of 5.0, when I thought the story and writing were even more compelling than in RED RISING, which I did give 5.0 stars. That's my story, and I'm sticking to it.<br><br>Bottom line: Read it, read it NOW. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/837199501" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Rising (Red Rising Trilogy, #1)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1165914522" rel="nofollow noopener">Morning Star (Red Rising Trilogy, #3)</a>
</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2202493786" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2202493786?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444759037" href="/book/show/25372230-golden-son">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2202493786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14035936551096298373"><i>“I will die. You will die. We will all die and the universe will carry on without care. All that we have is that shout into the wind - how we live. How we go. And how we stand before we fall.”</i><br/><br/>It’s been three days I finished <b>“Golden Son”</b> and I still don’t know how I <u>
  <b>feel</b>
</u> about it, let alone what I <u>
  <b>think</b>
</u> about it. >_< <br/>I’m just so confused and devastated and my heart is nothing but an empty void. <br/><br/>There seem to be three <u>bloodydamn</u> good reasons why I feel that way though:<br/><br/>1.)	Pierce Brown ripp</span>
  <span id="freeText14035936551096298373" style="display:none"><i>“I will die. You will die. We will all die and the universe will carry on without care. All that we have is that shout into the wind - how we live. How we go. And how we stand before we fall.”</i><br /><br />It’s been three days I finished <b>“Golden Son”</b> and I still don’t know how I <u>
  <b>feel</b>
</u> about it, let alone what I <u>
  <b>think</b>
</u> about it. &gt;_&lt; <br />I’m just so confused and devastated and my heart is nothing but an empty void. <br /><br />There seem to be three <u>bloodydamn</u> good reasons why I feel that way though:<br /><br />1.)	Pierce Brown ripped out my heart and gave it to the pitvipers.<br />2.)	He broke my mind and didn’t leave any glue.<br />3.)	His book shattered my soul and fractured it into tiny little pieces. <br /><br /><b>YES!</b> “Golden Son” quite literally destroyed me and I have no idea how I’m supposed to survive the third book. I got so attached to all those characters and whenever something happened to them, I almost got a heart attack. The pacing was so fast, I barely managed to keep up with all those many plot twists and every time I thought I knew in which direction it was heading, the entire story line changed once again. To read this book was like playing chess without any rules. *lol* You have all the familiar chess pieces you need in order to play a decent game of chess, but your nice little figures never do what they are actually meant to do. It’s like they constantly give you the finger instead! XD<br /><br />That’s so rude Pierce!! <br />So mean <br />and cruel <br />and painful!!! <br />You hear me?! <br /><b>SO FREAKING SAVAGE AND EXCRUCIATING!!!</b><br />*mental breakdown*<br /><br />Okay, okay I’m fine again. *clears throat* <br />Where was I again? Oh, yes the plot!<br /><br /><i>”How could so frail a girl have such a spirit, such a dream as freedom, when so many strong souls toiled and kept their heads down for fear of looking up?”</i><br /><br /><b>The plot:</b><br /><br /><i>”They say a kingdom divided against itself cannot stand. They made no mention of the heart.”</i><br /><br />After graduating from the Institute, Darrow Au Andromedus spent his last three years as a Lancer of House Augustus serving no other than Nero himself. Left to his own devices and without any guidance from Ares he didn’t just try his very best to find his way amongst his fellow Golds but also worked more than just hard to become an integral and important part of Nero’s forces. This however isn’t as easy as it seems and all it needs is a small mistake that’s able to destroy the good reputation he has built. After all there are plenty of enemies that want to get a piece of him, first and foremost Cassius au Bellona and his entire House which still holds a deadly grudge against him. With his loyal Howlers scattered all over the galaxy and only Roque at his side, the growing pressure on Darrow’s shoulders might soon become too strong to stand it any longer. Will he rise like a comet or will he tumble into red dirt?<br /><br /><i>”Your people. My people. We have languished in darkness. But there will come a day when we walk in the light. It will not come from their mercy. It will not come by fate. It will come when brave hearts rise and choose to break the chains, to live for more.”</i><br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><i>”We’re all just wounded souls, stumbling about in the dark, desperately trying to stitch ourselves together, hoping to fill the holes they ripped in us.”</i><br /><br /><u>
  <b>This is the moment you enter my spoiler section. There will be lots of quotes and information about the individual characters and most definitely also way too many subjective emotions for your own good! Don’t say I didn’t warn you! ;-P</b>
</u><br /><br /><b>Darrow:</b><br /><br /><i>”I’ve seen her hanged a thousand times now as her martyrdom spreads across the worlds, city by city. Yet each time, it strikes me like a physical blow, nerve endings shivering in my chest, heart beating fast, neck tight just under the jaw. How cruel a life, that the sight of my dead wife means hope.”</i><br /><br />Oh Darrow, my torn and insecure child! This boy is hurting so much, not just because of the things people are doing to him, but also because of his past, his current present and the things that might eventually happen in the future. He wears a burden that is too heavy for him but he still tries his best to stay strong, to keep on moving and to fight for the things he values. *sigh* He’s such a torn man, it’s exceptionally painful to watch. For instance Darrow still loves Eo and his family, but he also grew fond of some of his fellow Golds and to say he is walking a thin line between acceptance, betrayal and loyalty is actually putting it more than just mildly. In fact it doesn’t even get close to the truth! &gt;_&lt; That moment when he realised that Sevro knows about his true identity and accepts him the way he is, oh boy did it kill me!!! I was right there crying with him! &lt;333 Darrow has a too gentle soul for what he’s about to do, but his determination and will are incredible! XD I loved how he treated Mickey and I’m really sorry for what happened to the poor Carver. I mean just like Darrow he’s a product of his environment and he certainly didn’t deserve to be abused by Harmony. Still, as much as I admire Darrow he definitely made some huge mistakes as well and I think the ending of “Golden Son” made that more than just clear!!! Urgh that <b>ENDING!!</b> I can’t even… T_T<br /><br /><i>”In so many ways, I’m still a boy, lost and afraid, seeking warmth and love. When I feel dirt, I honor Eo. And when I see fire, I remember the warmth and flicker of the flames across Mustang’s skin as we lay in our chamber of ice and snow.”</i><br /><br /><i>”He can’t say any more because I’m hugging him and crying. I sob and hold on to him, shaking, scaring him. He doesn’t move except to pat me on the head. All the weight falls from my shoulders. Someone knows. He knows and he’s here. He knows and he came to help me. To help me. I can’t stop shaking and saying thank you. Eo was right. I was right. “You are my friend,” I tremble out like a child. It almost makes him cry seeing me this way.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Because you’re my friend.” I bring his hands to my lips, kissing them gently as he looks up at me with hopeful eyes. “Weird as you are, wicked as you were. I know you want to be better. You want to live for more. We all do. And there’s not a place they could take one of my friends that I would ever abandon them.”</i><br /><br /><b>Mustang:</b><br /><br /><i>”Shame you don’t respect me enough to suppose that I have my own plan. You think I’m here because my aching loins thrust me into Bellona arms. Please. I’m no bitch in heat. I protect my family by any means necessary. Who do you protect but yourself?”</i><br /><br />I don’t even dare to say it but I was kind of disappointed by Mustang in this book. I mean yes she’s still cheeky and she was one of the good guys, but after “Red Rising” I really would have expected her to play a more important role and to fight for her opinions and rights. First she decided to work for Octavia au Lune and then she became Cassius girlfriend?! Like seriously?! We all know what a - excuse my crude language - bitch Octavia is and to date Cassius because she thinks she might protect her family by doing so?! WTF!?!! Where is her fire?! Where is the snarky spark I loved so much?! She doesn’t have to resort to the typical tricks of a woman, she’s way better than that and the fact she chose to use her femininity instead of her strength, intelligence and will power was just frustrating. Truth be told I think Victra was a way better role model in this book! She didn’t care what others thought of her, she did what she wanted to and she took what she needed! Yup, I think I liked Victra more. *lol* Oh and don’t even get me started about Mustang’s reaction when she found out that Darrow is a Red!!! It’s like she wanted to support all the classes and change the system and then <b>BAM!</b> Darrow tells her he’s actually a Red and she hates him!? I mean yes she’s entitled to feel betrayed, everyone would do, but to react like that?! Preach water and drink wine, right?!<br /><br /><i>”If she gives me her heart, I’ll break it. My lie is too great to build a love upon. When she discovers what I am, she will reject me. Even if she could survive that, I would not.”</i><br /><br /><i>”The human spirit tries to break free, again and again, not in hate like the Dark Revolt. But for love. They don’t mimic each other. They aren’t inspired by others who come before them. Each is willing to take the leap, thinking they are the first. That’s bravery. And that means it’s part of who we are as people.”</i><br /><br /><b>Sevro:</b><br /><br /><i>”He stands quietly in his armor watching us, watching Roque hold the girl Sevro loves but has never told, the girl he could never have. The pain is raw and etched deep into the lines of his hawkish face. Impervious Sevro, immune to hurt, to sadness, to having his eye gouged out by Lilath, the Jackal’s lieutenant; it all falls on him now.”</i><br /><br />I still <b>L.O.V.E</b> that boy to bits and pieces!!! He’s truly the best thing about this series!!! &lt;333 Sevro is the best friend anyone can have and he’s so damn loyal and gentle it’s a pleasure to watch! Yes, I said gentle!! Because behind all his rabid-wolf-attitude and the tough façade he shows to others, he’s actually the sweetest and kindest soul ever! Plus I love his humour!!! XD And just like Darrow I seem to have a weakness for men with only one eye and a really sassy demeanour. (Yes Lucien I’m talking about YOU here!! ;-P) I wasn’t really surprised to find out that he’s half Red, I have to admit that Fitchner’s true identity threw me though. *lol* Who would have thought Fitchner had it in him? Well, I certainly didn’t! XD <br /><br /><i>”Audentes fortuna juvat,” Sevro chuckles. <br />“Fortune favors the bold? You deserve to die if that’s really going to be the last thing you say in this life.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Sevro?” I look around for him. He’s loitering around Pliny’s eyeball some twenty metres back. We turn to look at him and he shuffles his feet awkwardly.<br />”Can I …” He gestures to it.<br />“What?” Mustang asks.<br />“Can I have it?”<br />Mustang squints at him. “All yours.”<br />He scoops up the eyeball and jams it into his pocket, grinning merrily. He runs to catch up. “Collecting the set, hopefully.”</i><br /><br /><i>”I can’t do this without you.” After a desperate moment, “Are you with me? Sevro?”<br />He pulls back and wipes snot from his nose, muddying his face. Tears make lines in the mud as he looks up at me, voice cracking like a child’s. “Always, Darrow. Always.”</i><br /><br /><b>Roque:</b><br /><br /><i>”We are not our station in life. We are us – the sum of what we’ve done, what we want to do, and the people who we keep close. You’re my dearest friend, Darrow. Mind that. No matter what transpires, I will protect you as surely as you would protect me if ever I needed it.”</i><br /><br />Roque… my precious poet with principles. My kind spirit in a cruel world. <b>OH GOD, I CAN’T EVEN!!!</b> I knew this would come, I saw all the signs, Darrow’s betrayal, Quinn’s death, the fact Darrow shut him out of his inner circle over and over again. It was so damn hard to read!! Every little moment, every small action, every single word that left Darrow’s lips… it was poison for their friendship, poison for my poor Roque. Darrow should have tried to mend things between them, he should have given him time and an honest and long conversation but he did absolutely nothing and just left him out in the rain. Grief is a powerful emotion and it can change people in ways no one would have ever thought possible. Darrow of all people should have known this!!!! <b>DAMN IT!!!</b> Roque was so lonely and isolated, so broken… broken beyond repair and no one noticed. It’s really no surprise he did what he did…. I saw it coming, yet I still wasn’t prepared to face it. My heart is bleeding! <u>I AM HEARTBROKEN!</u> I feel so torn about Roque right now, but I can’t hate him. I can’t dislike him for what he did. He’s still my Roque. My gentle poet. *sobs* ARGH!! I hate Pierce Brown for making me feel this way. And how it happened in the end… I guess I finally have my answer how Roque made it through the passage…. I wish I would have never found out… It just hurts… T_T<br /><br /><i>”I didn’t mind that it was always about you, Darrow. That was what burned Tactus, but not me. I’m not in love with you like Mustang. I don’t worship you like Sevro or the Howlers. I was a true friend. I was someone who saw your light and your dark and accepted both without judgement, without agenda. And what did you do to me? You used me like a man uses a horse. I’m better than that. Quinn was better than that.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Friendships take minutes to make, moments to break, years to repair,” he says, turning to glance over his shoulder. “We’ll talk again soon.”</i><br /><br /><i>A needle from his ring pricks my wrist. Gentle, like the kiss he now plants on my cheek.<br />“And thus go liars, with a bloodydamn kiss.”<br />One word shatters a thousand lies.</i><br /><br /><b>The Jackal:</b><br /><br /><i>”Come now, Father …”<br />“You are not my son.”<br />Adrius flinches. With those few words, Augustus releases something. And the small part of Adrius that held out hope to be loved disappears. He shakes off his humanity, leaving only the Jackal.</i><br /><br />Cunning, cruel, conniving, relentless, heartless and creepy. In short: The perfect villain! Adrius is certainly a force to be reckoned with and this time around I actually truly and completely blame Darrow! He knew what he was getting himself into, he knew “The Jackal” wasn’t to be trusted, yet he still hoped his wrath wouldn’t reach him?! I mean what did he expect?! That the Jackal would stand aside while he became his father’s successor?! Didn’t the death of Leto teach him anything?! Adrius acted exactly the way I expected him to and I can’t believe Darrow actually fell for his trap! I don’t even want to know what he’s going to do with him… Knowing the Jackal it’s going to be cruel and savage though! &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />“Golden Son” was brilliant and ingenious! It caused me to laugh, it caused me to cry and it thoroughly broke my fragile heart! *sobs* I think I’ll never get over that ending… never ever as long as I live. It’s just too gorydamn painful! T_T<br /><br />This said, I actually must be a masochist because I really can’t wait to read the last book. *lol*<br />Thank you Pierce Brown, you successfully turned me into a sappy and weeping mess! ;-P</span>
  <a data-text-id="14035936551096298373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_889110975" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/889110975" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/889110975?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780345539816" href="/book/show/20697410-golden-son">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=really-looking-forward-to-this-book">really-looking-forward-to-this-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=epic">epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2014-favs">2014-favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=random-house">random-house</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer889110975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14984348633002011607">This 5 star rating might come as a surprised to some of you who know <a title='Review: Red Rising by Pierce Brown' href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/770718429?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>how conflicted <em>Red Rising</em> left me</a>. In fact, it's one of the only books I've read, but NOT rated. How often does that happen? Hmm... never. So how did I go from "unable to rate book one" to "loving book 2 something fierce"? The short and lazy answer is, I don't know. The long and complicated version is this review. Huzzah!<br/><br/><em>Golden Son</em> is a remarkable improvement over some of the issues I had with <em>Red Rising</em>. The writing and plot a</span>
  <span id="freeText14984348633002011607" style="display:none">This 5 star rating might come as a surprised to some of you who know <a title="Review: Red Rising by Pierce Brown" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/770718429?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">how conflicted <em>Red Rising</em> left me</a>. In fact, it's one of the only books I've read, but NOT rated. How often does that happen? Hmm... never. So how did I go from "unable to rate book one" to "loving book 2 something fierce"? The short and lazy answer is, I don't know. The long and complicated version is this review. Huzzah!<br><br><em>Golden Son</em> is a remarkable improvement over some of the issues I had with <em>Red Rising</em>. The writing and plot are noticeably stronger. The characters are fleshed out more. The action and suspense are cranked up several more notches. Really, I couldn't ask for more in a sequel.<br><br><strong>Fixed Issue #1: Super Slow Beginning</strong><br><br>First off, unlike <em>Red Rising</em> where I struggled with the first 100 pages, <em>Golden Son</em> starts off strong with plenty of action to keep the reader interested. Since the pesky job of world  building has been taken care of long, it gave Brown the opportunity to focus on what really mattered: making heads roll. What surprised me with <em>Golden Son</em> was just how many heads actually did roll, but more on that later.<br><br>The majority of this novel focuses on Darrow outside the academy and the war he purposefully started. We find out a lot more about the Sons of Ares and the inner workings of the politics of the Golds. I was a little wary about that because a ton of political intrigue can lead to boredom. But in this case, that was not something that ever happened.<br><br><strong>Fixed Issue #2: Treatment of Female Characters</strong><br><br>My biggest issue with <em>Red Rising</em> was the treatment of female characters, specifically Mustang. I felt she was put into deliberate situations that forced Darrow to swoop in and save her lest her virtue be ruined. I'm so over that trope in books, so I was disappointed to see it in Red Rising.<br><br>The good news is that Brown clearly took more care with showing us Mustang's strength. (slight spoilers, but not really) There's one scene in <em>Golden Son</em> where Darrow finally has a chance to talk to Mustang after certain events have pulled them apart and she ends up close with Cassius. He claims that he understands how she must feel, but she quickly corrects him. This is my favorite scene in the entire book:<br><blockquote>"Now, I'm sure you understand that I felt lost. One, because I thought I'd found someone special in you. Two, because I felt you were abandoning the idea that gave us the ability to conquer Olympus. Consider that I was vulnerable. Lonely. And that perhaps I fell into Cassius's bed because I was hurt and needed a salve to my pain. Can you imagine that? You may answer."<br><br>I squirm on my cushion. "I suppose."<br><br>"Good. Now shove that idea up your ass." Her lips make a hard line. "I am not some frill-wearing tramp. I am a genius. I say this because it is a fact. I am smarter than any person you've met, except perhaps my twin. My heart does not make my brain a fool."</blockquote><br>I really love how confident Mustang is in that scene and how unashamed she is about it. In that same scene, she goes on to tell him that he is not as invincible as he thinks and how he needs her if he has any hope of winning the war.<br><br>I just really wished Darrow listened more. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ If there was one thing that I had issue with, it's that if Darrow had repaired his friendship with Roque, none of the events in the ending would have happened. Servo and Mustang kept telling him over and over, "Fix that, Darrow" and he would agree, but never makes strides to actually do it. I just wanted to shake him and say, "You are at war! You need all your allies to be completely on your side!!" My problem was that the foreshadowing for that was too obvious. I knew that eventually it would lead to something devastating. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><strong>Fixed Issue #3: Darrow's a Super Gary Stu</strong><br><br>This can't be denied. No matter how much I admit to liking <em>Red Rising</em>, there was no doubt about it: Darrow was a Gary Stu in every possible way. He's The One. The Only One who can bring down the Golds and help the Reds rise. He can overcome any situation, no matter how horrible or impossible. I can completely see why this may bother some readers even if the novel contains intense fight scenes and dramatic rescues. It just gets to a point where you start to say, "COME ON ALREADY."<br><br><em>Golden Son</em> completely crushes that. Right from the first scene in the book, we see Darrow failing at something important and non one wants anything to do with him besides Roque. It was a little jarring to see Darrow that low, considering how far he had fallen. But shortly after, Brown played an interesting hand that *somewhat* annoyed me and the Gary Stu-ness returned in Full Gundam Force. However, just like in <em>Red Rising</em>, this didn't bother me much because I was too focused on fact that Darrow was busy giving someone the ass beating of a lifetime. What can I say? Priorities, I've got them.<br><br>What's interesting is how the other characters continually call Darrow out on his apparent invincibility several times. My favorite one being this quote:<br><blockquote>“You are but a mortal," Roque whispers in my ear, riding his horse alongside the chariot, as per tradition.<br>"And a whorefart," Servo calls from the other side.<br>"Yes," Roque agrees solemnly. "That too.”</blockquote><br><strong>OMG THE ENDING THO.</strong><br><br>When the ending finally came, I realized Brown had me right where he wanted me (get your minds out of the gutter). After thinking that Darrow could pull through out of anything that opposed him, I was not prepared for the ending. Truly, the last 25% of this novel is what bumped my rating from 4 starts to 5. There was so much death in that scene that it made <em>Red Rising</em> look like child's play. And that took balls. It made me angry, shocked, confused and immensely distraught. I absolutely have no idea how Darrow is supposed to pull through this mess. It's that bad.<br><br>My feelings are so conflicted about the ending, it can only be described by way of Kanye and Jay-Z lyrics.<br><br>Ball so hard.<br>Dat shit cray.<br>BITCH BEHAVE.<br><br>Then there's my ship. Mustang and The Reaper. I really need this to work out. This is my OTP. My ship that I might just go down with. Unfortunately, Brown hasn't said anything to calm my fears and I'm sitting on the edge of my seat in fear.<br><br><a href="https://twitter.com/Pierce_Brown/status/542160533458149377" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422906102i/13562012._SX540_.png" alt=" photo Screen Shot 2015-02-02 at 2.31.57 PM_zpszmnmaqep.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Bloodydamn.<br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery</a>.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="14984348633002011607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
