<div id="review_1030814593" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1030814593" />
    <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata"><img alt="Faye, la Patata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557835753p2/7650833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1030814593?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=depressing-as-hell">depressing-as-hell</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=dark-and-gritty">dark-and-gritty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=space">space</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=conspiracies">conspiracies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=haunting-narration">haunting-narration</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=good-hero">good-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1030814593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15455316195380564917"><b>EDIT:</b> just finished this bloodydamn good book for the second time and I am completely shattered, wrecked, and in absolute overwhelming despair. How? How does this author write so amazingly that his words and narrative rip you apart from all directions? Throughout reading, I was high then I was low, from feeling the glory to feeling the pain and anguish. Seriously, I am not sure I can survive from this. BRAVO!!!<br/><br/><br/><strong>If you've come here upon the assumption that I am able to talk about my feelings for t</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText15455316195380564917" style="display:none"><b>EDIT:</b> just finished this bloodydamn good book for the second time and I am completely shattered, wrecked, and in absolute overwhelming despair. How? How does this author write so amazingly that his words and narrative rip you apart from all directions? Throughout reading, I was high then I was low, from feeling the glory to feeling the pain and anguish. Seriously, I am not sure I can survive from this. BRAVO!!!<br><br><br><strong>If you've come here upon the assumption that I am able to talk about my feelings for this book coherently, I am sorry to say but your expectations have been for naught.</strong> How can I be coherent when this book turned my life upside down? While reading this book from start to finish, I have shamelessly done the following:<br><br>1.) Roll on the bed over and over, with eyes cracked open, fearing for the well-being of my precious Darrow;<br>2.) Howl like a hyena at Darrow's glorious moments;<br>3.) Bang my head on the wall to relieve some of the stress this book has given me,BECAUSE OMG OMG OMG DARROW OMG OMG OMG MUSTANG OMG OMG OMG SEVRO LORN AND EVERYONE ELSE OMG OMG OMG!!!<br>4.) Rinse and repeat<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421436247ra/13376096.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*sips tea* *looks at you with a raised eyebrow*<br><br>However, despite the off-chance that your impression of me now has changed (and I wouldn't blame you; I would think myself a mad lunatic, too. Surely a small price to pay to read a bloodydamn good book?), I wouldn't change any of it, coherent or not. <strong>When I read <em>Red Rising</em> last year, I've thought that succeeding books would have a hard time toppling it.</strong> It was <em>the</em> book that made me believe in these genres again, <em>the</em> book that rekindled my love for reading, <em>the </em>book that made me see red of the social injustice that exactly mirror the plights billions of people here on Earth experience every <em>single</em> day.<br><br><strong>And then came <em>Golden Son</em>.</strong><br><br>Very well, I'll explain my insights as coherent as I can.<br><br>If <em>Red Rising</em> made the genre alive again, the second installment was the one who put the bar higher than ever before. It's <strong>more brutal, more heart-breaking, more shocking, and even more glorious</strong>. You read this and it's like watching ancient Romans battle it out with conquest and diplomacy in space. I am fucking serious. If ever there were a space opera with Julius Caesar in it, <em>this book would be <strong>it. </strong></em>It's highly engaging and visualizing, making you angry, sad, and teary-eyed while pumping you adrenaline every step of the way, because baby, this is as unpredictable as it can get.<strong> I'm not surprised this has a film in the making - it has the formula down pat.</strong><br><br><strong>I absolutely love Darrow in this one.</strong> There were times he seemed like a whiny baby (especially at the beginning... "No, I must take this path." "I was wrong, the path I've taken sucks." "Yes, I will take this other path!" "Gosh darnit, wrong again... let me cry a bit over here..." Obviously non-verbatim, but you get the point, yes?), but all these things only added to his complexity over what he feels is needed to be done to tame a hungry society that has been dead-set on a selfish mentality for centuries. <strong>What's a man to do when to fight the fire he must fight it with fire as well?</strong> A double-edged sword surely, because you end up fanning the flames, but it was so interesting and heart-breaking seeing him be torn of doing one thing and wanting to do the other. <strong>He pulls you into his misery, making you feel despair alongside him as he mulls over the morality of the people surrounding him and his own.</strong> You feel and see the horrors he face, pushing you into a pit of overwhelming emotions.<br><br><strong>So brutal and horrible, yet so mystifying and beautiful at the same time.</strong> I don't have any dobut that more than the setting, it's Darrow and how he stands up against the social injustice of the Golds and their mentality that truly makes this book shine.<br><br>And the twists! Holy heavens above, they pierced the feels where they hurt. I never saw them coming. Of course, I expected that Darrow will eventually face harder obstacles along the way, but I never expected them to be of great magnitude. I was <strong>crushed</strong> by the end. I was crying and in denial. <strong>But despite all the cursing and wailing that followed, it were the very same events that made me feel this book was truly magical and epic.</strong><br><br>I really don't know what else to say beyond what I have already said and what has already been said around the blogosphere. If you're the type of person who don't buy hypes, I implore you to take one exception and take this on, because rarely do you get a book this good.<br><br><br><b>IMMEDIATELY AFTER READING:</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421316024ra/13358001.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>HOLY SHEEET<br>HOLY SHEEET<br>HOLY GUACAMOLE SHEEEEEEEET</b><br><br>FUCKFUCKFUCKFUCKFUCKFUCKFUCKFUCK<br><br>I'M DONE. I'M DEAD. THIS BOOK KILLED ME.<br><br><b>I FEEL LIKE I JUST WATCHED A DRAMA SET IN ANCIENT ROME - FULL OF LIES, BETRAYALS, AND CONSPIRACIES.</b><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15455316195380564917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dR9jBdZt4U9KK/IuKfyYM7QPQdXNl0cQ95i37lzNETVZ/SjZV9Xasek+QGMEigpFX7appc+zgcXyfv7l97IpYQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7ZyuLpigx6hwhgW9ZzLMFy7oshV6EgjT27/ZVLQXkFXBfuXyGRj8VtOTt/BKRF5hxVFaZXg2zgbeWZBfH2ioAQ==')})
  }
